War">Syrian Civil War</a> that reportedly includes an <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">al-Qaeda</a> linked <a href="/wiki/Al-Nusra_Front" title="Al-Nusra Front">al-Nusra Front</a> and another <a href="/wiki/Salafi_jihadism" title="Salafi jihadism">Salafi</a> coalition known as <a href="/wiki/Ahrar_ash-Sham" class="mw-redirect" title="Ahrar ash-Sham">Ahrar ash-Sham</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ISIS_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ISIS-153">[153]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a>, Qatar supported the first ever democratically elected Islamist <sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> <sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> President <a href="/wiki/Mohamed_Morsi" title="Mohamed Morsi">Mohamed Morsi</a> via diplomatic support and the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a> network until he was overthrown by a <a href="/wiki/2013_Egyptian_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2013 Egyptian coup d'état">military coup d'état</a> in July 2013 following <a href="/wiki/June_2013_Egyptian_protests" title="June 2013 Egyptian protests">mass protests</a> against his rule.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FP_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FP-160">[160]</a></sup> Qatar offered Egypt a $7.5 billion loan during the year he was in power.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar's alignment with <a href="/wiki/Hamas" title="Hamas">Hamas</a>, first reported in early 2012,<sup id="cite_ref-bbchamas_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbchamas-162">[162]</a></sup> has drawn criticism from Israel, the United States, Egypt and Saudi Arabia, "who accuse Qatar of undermining regional stability by supporting Hamas."<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> The Foreign Minister of Qatar has denied supporting Hamas, saying that the country "[does] not support Hamas[,] but support[s] the Palestinians."<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Following a peace agreement, Qatar pledged $1 billion in humanitarian aid to Gaza.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Combined_Air_Operations_Center_151007-F-MS415-019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Combined_Air_Operations_Center_151007-F-MS415-019.jpg/220px-Combined_Air_Operations_Center_151007-F-MS415-019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Combined_Air_Operations_Center_151007-F-MS415-019.jpg/330px-Combined_Air_Operations_Center_151007-F-MS415-019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Combined_Air_Operations_Center_151007-F-MS415-019.jpg/440px-Combined_Air_Operations_Center_151007-F-MS415-019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Combined_Air_Operations_Center_151007-F-MS415-019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The US Combined <a href="/wiki/Air_and_Space_Operations_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Air and Space Operations Center">Air and Space Operations Center</a> (CAOC) at <a href="/wiki/Al_Udeid_Air_Base" title="Al Udeid Air Base">Al Udeid Air Base</a> provides command and control of air power throughout <a href="/wiki/Iraq" title="Iraq">Iraq</a>, <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">Afghanistan</a>, and 17 other nations.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Qatar has hosted academic, religious, political, and economic conferences. The 11th annual Doha Forum recently brought in key thinkers, professionals of various backgrounds, and political figures from all over the world to discuss democracy, media and information technology, free trade, and <a href="/wiki/Water_security" title="Water security">water security</a> issues. In addition, the forum has featured the Middle East Economic Future conference since 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> In more recent times, Qatar has hosted peace talks between rival factions across the globe. Notable among these include the Darfur Agreement. The Doha Declaration is the basis of the peace process in Darfur and it has achieved significant gains on the ground for the African region. Notable achievements included the restoration of security and stability, progress made in construction and reconstruction processes, return of displaced residents and uniting of Darfur people to face challenges and push forward the peace process.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup> Qatar donated £88.5million in funds to finance recovery and reconstruction in Darfur.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2017, Saudi Arabia, the UAE, Bahrain, Egypt and Yemen <a href="/wiki/2017_Qatar_diplomatic_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="2017 Qatar diplomatic crisis">broke diplomatic ties</a> with Qatar, accusing Qatar of <a href="/wiki/Qatar_and_state-sponsored_terrorism" title="Qatar and state-sponsored terrorism">supporting terrorism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> escalating a dispute over Qatar's support of the <a href="/wiki/Muslim_Brotherhood" title="Muslim Brotherhood">Muslim Brotherhood</a>, considered a terrorist organization by those five Arab nations.<sup id="cite_ref-guard_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard-170">[170]</a></sup> Saudi Arabia explained the move to be a necessary measure in protecting the kingdom's security. Qatari troops were also removed from the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">military coalition in Yemen</a>. Egypt closed its airspace and seaports to all Qatari transportation.<sup id="cite_ref-guard_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guard-170">[170]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2018, Saudi Arabia announced a bid to construct a waterway, <a href="/wiki/Salwa_Canal" title="Salwa Canal">Salwa Canal</a>, on their border with Qatar which shall in effect turn the latter into an <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Two years after the diplomatic crisis, <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> took a step towards restoring its relations with Qatar. In July 2019, <a href="/wiki/Amman" title="Amman">Amman</a> appointed a new ambassador to Qatar, who had been withdrawn in 2017 in support of the Gulf-Arab allies.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Armed_Forces" title="Qatar Armed Forces">Qatar Armed Forces</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2170" data-file-height="1346"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Dassault_Mirage_2000-5_participating_in_Odyssey_Dawn_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Qatari <a href="/wiki/Dassault_Mirage_2000" title="Dassault Mirage 2000">Dassault Mirage 2000</a> flying over <a href="/wiki/Libya" title="Libya">Libya</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Qatar Armed Forces are the military forces of Qatar. The country maintains a modest military force of approximately 11,800 men, including an army (8,500), navy (1,800) and air force (1,500). Qatar's defense expenditures accounted for approximately 4.2% of gross national product in 1993, and 1.5% of gross domestic product in 2010, the most recent year available in the SIPRI statistical database.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup> Qatar has recently signed defense pacts with the United States and United Kingdom, as well as with France earlier in 1994. Qatar plays an active role in the collective defense efforts of the <a href="/wiki/Cooperation_Council_for_the_Arab_States_of_the_Gulf" class="mw-redirect" title="Cooperation Council for the Arab States of the Gulf">Gulf Cooperation Council</a>; the other five members are Saudi Arabia, Kuwait, Bahrain, the UAE, and Oman. The presence of the large <a href="/wiki/Al_Udeid_Air_Base" title="Al Udeid Air Base">Al Udeid Air Base</a>, operated by the United States and several other UN nations, provides a guaranteed source of defense and national security. In 2008 Qatar spent US$2.3 billion on military expenditures, 2.3% of the gross domestic product.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> Qatari special forces have been trained by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and other Western countries, and are believed to possess considerable skill.<sup id="cite_ref-strangepow_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strangepow-179">[179]</a></sup> They also helped the Libyan rebels during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tripoli_(2011)" title="Battle of Tripoli (2011)">2011 Battle of Tripoli</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-strangepow_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strangepow-179">[179]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:US,_allied_armed_forces_respond_to_terrorist_threat_scenario_130428-F-CJ989-005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/US%2C_allied_armed_forces_respond_to_terrorist_threat_scenario_130428-F-CJ989-005.jpg/220px-US%2C_allied_armed_forces_respond_to_terrorist_threat_scenario_130428-F-CJ989-005.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/US%2C_allied_armed_forces_respond_to_terrorist_threat_scenario_130428-F-CJ989-005.jpg/330px-US%2C_allied_armed_forces_respond_to_terrorist_threat_scenario_130428-F-CJ989-005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/US%2C_allied_armed_forces_respond_to_terrorist_threat_scenario_130428-F-CJ989-005.jpg/440px-US%2C_allied_armed_forces_respond_to_terrorist_threat_scenario_130428-F-CJ989-005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:US,_allied_armed_forces_respond_to_terrorist_threat_scenario_130428-F-CJ989-005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Qatar Armed Forces during joint exercises with the U.S. military
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Stockholm_International_Peace_Research_Institute" title="Stockholm International Peace Research Institute">Stockholm International Peace Research Institute</a> (SIPRI) found that in 2010–14 Qatar was the 46th-largest arms importer in the world. SIPRI writes that Qatar's plans to transform and significantly enlarge its armed forces have accelerated. Orders in 2013 for 62 tanks and 24 self-propelled guns from Germany were followed in 2014 by a number of other contracts, including 24 combat helicopters and 3 <a href="/wiki/Airborne_early_warning_and_control" title="Airborne early warning and control">early-warning-and-control</a> aircraft from the US, and 2 tanker aircraft from Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup> In 2015, Qatar was the 16th largest arms importer in the world, and in 2016, it was the 11th largest, according to SIPRI.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar's military participated in the <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabian-led_intervention_in_Yemen" title="Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen">Saudi Arabian-led intervention in Yemen</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia</a> <a href="/wiki/Houthis" class="mw-redirect" title="Houthis">Houthis</a>. In 2015, <i>Al Jazeera America</i> reported: "Numerous reports suggest that the Saudi-led coalition against opposition groups in Yemen has indiscriminately attacked civilians and used cluster bombs in civilian-populated areas, in violation of international law."<sup id="cite_ref-aljazeeraus201512_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aljazeeraus201512-182">[182]</a></sup> Many civilians have been killed and the large parts of the infrastructure in this region is now destroyed.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup> Hospitals have also been bombed by the Saudis and those operating with them.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> Qatar was suspended from the coalition in Yemen due to the 2017 <a href="/wiki/Qatar_diplomatic_crisis" title="Qatar diplomatic crisis">Qatar diplomatic crisis</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Qatar" title="Human rights in Qatar">Human rights in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Treatment_of_South_Asian_labourers_in_the_Gulf_Cooperation_Council_region" title="Treatment of South Asian labourers in the Gulf Cooperation Council region">Treatment of South Asian labourers in the Gulf Cooperation Council region</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Migrant_workers_in_West_Bay_Doha.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Migrant_workers_in_West_Bay_Doha.jpg/220px-Migrant_workers_in_West_Bay_Doha.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Migrant_workers_in_West_Bay_Doha.jpg/330px-Migrant_workers_in_West_Bay_Doha.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Migrant_workers_in_West_Bay_Doha.jpg/440px-Migrant_workers_in_West_Bay_Doha.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1074"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Migrant_workers_in_West_Bay_Doha.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Migrant workers in Doha.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>According to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">U.S. State Department</a>, expatriate workers from nations throughout <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a> voluntarily migrate to Qatar as low-skilled labourers or domestic servants, but some subsequently face conditions indicative of involuntary servitude. Some of the more common labour rights violations include beatings, withholding of payment, charging workers for benefits for which the employer is responsible, restrictions on freedom of movement (such as the confiscation of passports, travel documents, or exit permits), arbitrary detention, threats of legal action, and sexual assault.<sup id="cite_ref-2011narrq_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011narrq-186">[186]</a></sup> Many migrant workers arriving for work in Qatar have paid exorbitant fees to recruiters in their home countries.<sup id="cite_ref-2011narrq_186-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011narrq-186">[186]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, certain provisions of the Qatari Criminal Code allows punishments such as <a href="/wiki/Flogging" class="mw-redirect" title="Flogging">flogging</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stoning" title="Stoning">stoning</a> to be imposed as criminal sanctions. The <a href="/wiki/UN_Committee_Against_Torture" class="mw-redirect" title="UN Committee Against Torture">UN Committee Against Torture</a> found that these practices constituted a breach of the obligations imposed by the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Convention_Against_Torture" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Convention Against Torture">UN Convention Against Torture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> Qatar retains the death penalty, mainly for threats against national security such as terrorism. The use of the death penalty is rare and no state executions have taken place in Qatar since 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> In Qatar, <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Qatar" title="LGBT rights in Qatar">homosexual acts</a> are illegal and can be <a href="/wiki/Death_penalty_for_homosexuality" class="mw-redirect" title="Death penalty for homosexuality">punished by death</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Under the provisions of Qatar's sponsorship law, sponsors have the unilateral power to cancel workers' residency permits, deny workers' ability to change employers, report a worker as "absconded" to police authorities, and deny permission to leave the country.<sup id="cite_ref-2011narrq_186-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011narrq-186">[186]</a></sup> As a result, sponsors may restrict workers' movements and workers may be afraid to report abuses or claim their rights.<sup id="cite_ref-2011narrq_186-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011narrq-186">[186]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/ITUC" class="mw-redirect" title="ITUC">ITUC</a>, the visa sponsorship system allows the exaction of <a href="/wiki/Forced_labour" title="Forced labour">forced labour</a> by making it difficult for a migrant worker to leave an abusive employer or travel overseas without permission.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup> Qatar also does not maintain wage standards for its <a href="/wiki/Immigrant" class="mw-redirect" title="Immigrant">immigrant</a> labourers. Qatar commissioned international law firm <a href="/wiki/DLA_Piper" title="DLA Piper">DLA Piper</a> to produce a report investigating the immigrant labour system. In May 2014 DLA Piper released over 60 recommendations for reforming the kafala system including the abolition of exit visas and the introduction of a minimum wage which Qatar has pledged to implement.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Labour_Organization" title="International Labour Organization">International Labour Organization</a> (ILO), a minimum wage entered into force for any worker of all nationalities and in all sectors in Qatar on 20 March 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 2012, Qatari officials declared their intention to allow the establishment of an independent trade union.<sup id="cite_ref-unions_194-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unions-194">[194]</a></sup> Qatar also announced it would scrap its sponsor system for foreign labour, which requires that all <a href="/wiki/Migrant_workers_in_the_Gulf_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Migrant workers in the Gulf region">foreign workers</a> be sponsored by local employers.<sup id="cite_ref-unions_194-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unions-194">[194]</a></sup> Additional changes to labour laws include a provision guaranteeing that all workers' salaries are paid directly into their bank accounts and new restrictions on working outdoors in the hottest hours during the summer.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[195]</a></sup> New draft legislation announced in early 2015 mandates that companies that fail to pay workers' wages on time could temporarily lose their ability to hire more employees.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[196]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In October 2015 Qatar's Emir signed into law new reforms to the country's sponsorship system, with the new law taking effect within one year.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[197]</a></sup> Critics claim that the changes could fail to address some labour rights issues.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[198]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[199]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country enfranchised women at the same time as men in connection with the 1999 elections for a Central Municipal Council.<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert2011a_108-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert2011a-108">[108]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[200]</a></sup> These elections—the first-ever in Qatar—were deliberately held on 8 March 1999, <a href="/wiki/International_Women%27s_Day" title="International Women's Day">International Women's Day</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lambert2011a_108-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lambert2011a-108">[108]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In July 2019, UN ambassadors of 37 countries, including Qatar, Bahrain and Saudi Arabia, have signed a joint letter to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Human_Rights_Council" title="United Nations Human Rights Council">UNHRC</a> defending China's <a href="/wiki/Xinjiang_re-education_camps" class="mw-redirect" title="Xinjiang re-education camps">treatment of Uyghurs</a> and other Muslim ethnic minorities.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[201]</a></sup> However, in August 2019, Qatar told the UNHRC president that it decided to withdraw from the joint letter.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[202]</a></sup> Human rights activists praised Qatar's decision.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[203]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Qatar" title="Municipalities of Qatar">Municipalities of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Qatar,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored_2015.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored_2015.svg/220px-Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored_2015.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="209" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored_2015.svg/330px-Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored_2015.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored_2015.svg/440px-Qatar%2C_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored_2015.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1039" data-file-height="987"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Qatar,_administrative_divisions_-_Nmbrs_-_colored_2015.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Municipalities of Qatar as of 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 2014, Qatar has been divided into eight municipalities (Arabic: <a href="/wiki/Baladiyah" title="Baladiyah">baladiyah</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[204]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ol>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Shamal" title="Al Shamal">Al Shamal</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Khor_(municipality)" class="mw-redirect" title="Al Khor (municipality)">Al Khor</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al-Shahaniya" title="Al-Shahaniya">Al-Shahaniya</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Umm_Salal" title="Umm Salal">Umm Salal</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Daayen" title="Al Daayen">Al Daayen</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Ad-Dawhah_(municipality)" title="Ad-Dawhah (municipality)">Doha</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Rayyan" title="Al Rayyan">Al Rayyan</a></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Wakrah_(municipality)" title="Al Wakrah (municipality)">Al Wakrah</a></li>
      </ol> 
      <p>For statistical purposes, the municipalities are further subdivided into 98 <a href="/wiki/Zones_of_Qatar" title="Zones of Qatar">zones</a> (as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>),<sup id="cite_ref-2015census_205-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2015census-205">[205]</a></sup> which are in turn subdivided into blocks.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[206]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_municipalities">Former municipalities</span></h3> 
      <ul>
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Jemailiya" title="Al Jemailiya">Al Jemailiya</a> (until 2004)<sup id="cite_ref-2004census_207-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004census-207">[207]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Al_Ghuwariyah" title="Al Ghuwariyah">Al Ghuwariyah</a> (until 2004)<sup id="cite_ref-2004census_207-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004census-207">[207]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Jariyan_al_Batnah" class="mw-redirect" title="Jariyan al Batnah">Jariyan al Batnah</a> (until 2004)<sup id="cite_ref-2004census_207-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2004census-207">[207]</a></sup></li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Mesaieed" title="Mesaieed">Mesaieed</a> (<a href="/wiki/Umm_Sa%27id" class="mw-redirect" title="Umm Sa'id">Umm Sa'id</a>) (until 2006)<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[208]</a></sup></li>
      </ul> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Qatar" title="Geography of Qatar">Geography of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:194px;max-width:194px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Desert_Coast_(6996854733).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Desert_Coast_%286996854733%29.jpg/192px-Desert_Coast_%286996854733%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="192" height="128" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Desert_Coast_%286996854733%29.jpg/288px-Desert_Coast_%286996854733%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Desert_Coast_%286996854733%29.jpg/384px-Desert_Coast_%286996854733%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Desert coast
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:194px;max-width:194px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:127px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Desert_Qatar.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Desert_Qatar.JPG/192px-Desert_Qatar.JPG" decoding="async" width="192" height="127" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Desert_Qatar.JPG/288px-Desert_Qatar.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f5/Desert_Qatar.JPG/384px-Desert_Qatar.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1544" data-file-height="1024"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Desert landscape in Qatar
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Qatari <a href="/wiki/Peninsula" title="Peninsula">peninsula</a> protrudes 160 kilometres (100&nbsp;mi) into the Persian Gulf, north of Saudi Arabia. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/24th_parallel_north" title="24th parallel north">24°</a> and <a href="/wiki/27th_parallel_north" title="27th parallel north">27° N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/50th_meridian_east" title="50th meridian east">50°</a> and <a href="/wiki/52nd_meridian_east" title="52nd meridian east">52° E</a>. Most of the country consists of a low, barren <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plain</a>, covered with <a href="/wiki/Sand" title="Sand">sand</a>. To the southeast lies the <a href="/wiki/Khor_al_Adaid" class="mw-redirect" title="Khor al Adaid">Khor al&nbsp;Adaid</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Inland_sea_(geology)" title="Inland sea (geology)">Inland Sea</a>"), an area of rolling sand dunes surrounding an <a href="/wiki/Inlet" title="Inlet">inlet</a> of the Persian Gulf. There are mild winters and very hot, humid summers. </p>
      <p>The highest point in Qatar is Qurayn Abu al Bawl at 103 metres (338&nbsp;ft)<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-2">[2]</a></sup> in the Jebel Dukhan to the west, a range of low <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a> <a href="/wiki/Outcrop" title="Outcrop">outcroppings</a> running north–south from Zikrit through <a href="/wiki/Umm_Bab" title="Umm Bab">Umm Bab</a> to the southern border. The Jebel Dukhan area also contains Qatar's main onshore <a href="/wiki/Oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Oil field">oil deposits</a>, while the <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Natural gas field">natural gas fields</a> lie offshore, to the northwest of the peninsula. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Biodiversity_and_environment">Biodiversity and environment</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Wildlife_of_Qatar" title="Wildlife of Qatar">Wildlife of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">
      <div class="thumb tmulti tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:392px;max-width:392px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:205px;max-width:205px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:135px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Arabian_oryx_(oryx_leucoryx).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Arabian_oryx_%28oryx_leucoryx%29.jpg/203px-Arabian_oryx_%28oryx_leucoryx%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="203" height="135" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Arabian_oryx_%28oryx_leucoryx%29.jpg/305px-Arabian_oryx_%28oryx_leucoryx%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Arabian_oryx_%28oryx_leucoryx%29.jpg/406px-Arabian_oryx_%28oryx_leucoryx%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3638" data-file-height="2425"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <a href="/wiki/Arabian_oryx" title="Arabian oryx">Arabian oryx</a>, the national animal of Qatar
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:183px;max-width:183px">
          <div class="thumbimage" style="height:135px;overflow:hidden">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Qatari_ostriches_(3206781575).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Qatari_ostriches_%283206781575%29.jpg/181px-Qatari_ostriches_%283206781575%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="181" height="136" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Qatari_ostriches_%283206781575%29.jpg/272px-Qatari_ostriches_%283206781575%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Qatari_ostriches_%283206781575%29.jpg/362px-Qatari_ostriches_%283206781575%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           Ostriches in Qatar
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Qatar signed the Rio <a href="/wiki/Convention_on_Biological_Diversity" title="Convention on Biological Diversity">Convention on Biological Diversity</a> on 11 June 1992, and became a party to the convention on 21 August 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[209]</a></sup> It has subsequently produced a <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity_Action_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Biodiversity Action Plan">National Biodiversity Strategy and Action Plan</a>, which was received by the convention on 18 May 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[210]</a></sup> A total of 142 fungal species have been recorded from Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[211]</a></sup> A book recently produced by the Ministry of Environment documents the <a href="/wiki/Lizards" class="mw-redirect" title="Lizards">lizards</a> known or believed to occur in Qatar, based on surveys conducted by an international team of scientists and other collaborators.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[212]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the Emissions Database for Global Atmospheric Research, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_carbon_dioxide_emissions_per_capita" title="List of countries by carbon dioxide emissions per capita">carbon dioxide emissions per person</a> average over 30 tonnes, one of the highest in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[213]</a></sup> Qataris are also some of the highest consumers of water per capita per day, using around 400&nbsp;litres.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[214]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008 Qatar launched its <a href="/wiki/Qatar_National_Vision_2030" title="Qatar National Vision 2030">National Vision 2030</a> which highlights environmental development as one of the four main goals for Qatar over the next two decades. The National Vision pledges to develop sustainable alternatives to oil-based energy to preserve the local and global environment.<sup id="cite_ref-Qatar_National_Vision_2030_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Qatar_National_Vision_2030-215">[215]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Qatar" title="Economy of Qatar">Economy of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Doha_City,_UNCTAD_XIII_(7115124733).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Doha_City%2C_UNCTAD_XIII_%287115124733%29.jpg/220px-Doha_City%2C_UNCTAD_XIII_%287115124733%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Doha_City%2C_UNCTAD_XIII_%287115124733%29.jpg/330px-Doha_City%2C_UNCTAD_XIII_%287115124733%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Doha_City%2C_UNCTAD_XIII_%287115124733%29.jpg/440px-Doha_City%2C_UNCTAD_XIII_%287115124733%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2023"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Doha_City,_UNCTAD_XIII_(7115124733).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Commercial district in Doha.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Before the discovery of oil, the economy of the Qatari region focused on fishing and <a href="/wiki/Pearl_hunting" title="Pearl hunting">pearl hunting</a>. A report prepared by local governors of Ottoman Empire in 1892 states that total income from pearl hunting in 1892 is 2,450,000 kran.<sup id="cite_ref-Fromhertz2012_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fromhertz2012-73">[73]</a></sup> After the introduction of the Japanese <a href="/wiki/Cultured_pearl" title="Cultured pearl">cultured pearl</a> onto the world market in the 1920s and 1930s, Qatar's pearling industry crashed. Oil was discovered in Qatar in 1940, in <a href="/wiki/Dukhan_Field" title="Dukhan Field">Dukhan Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-emboil_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-emboil-216">[216]</a></sup> The discovery transformed the state's economy. Now, the country has a high <a href="/wiki/Standard_of_living" title="Standard of living">standard of living</a> for its legal citizens. With no <a href="/wiki/Income_tax" title="Income tax">income tax</a>, Qatar (along with <a href="/wiki/Bahrain" title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>) is one of the countries with the lowest tax rates in the world. The unemployment rate in June 2013 was 0.1%.<sup id="cite_ref-newhopenyt_217-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newhopenyt-217">[217]</a></sup> Corporate law mandates that Qatari nationals must hold 51% of any venture in the emirate.<sup id="cite_ref-nobs_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nobs-91">[91]</a></sup> Trade and industry in the emirate is overseen by the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Business_and_Trade_(Qatar)" title="Ministry of Business and Trade (Qatar)">Ministry of Business and Trade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">[218]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>As of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Qatar has the fourth highest GDP per capita in the world, according to the International Monetary Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-imfoct_219-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-imfoct-219">[219]</a></sup> It relies heavily on foreign labor to grow its economy, to the extent that <a href="/wiki/Migrant_worker" title="Migrant worker">migrant workers</a> compose 86% of the population and 94% of the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">[220]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">[221]</a></sup> Qatar has been criticized by the <a href="/wiki/International_Trade_Union_Confederation" title="International Trade Union Confederation">International Trade Union Confederation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">[222]</a></sup> The economic growth of Qatar has been almost exclusively based on its petroleum and natural gas industries, which began in 1940.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">[223]</a></sup> Qatar is the leading exporter of <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">liquefied natural gas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-strangepow_179-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strangepow-179">[179]</a></sup> In 2012, it was estimated that Qatar would invest over $120&nbsp;billion in the energy sector in the next 10 years.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">[224]</a></sup> The country was a member state of <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">Organization of Petroleum Exporting Countries</a> (OPEC), having joined in 1961, and having left in January 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">[225]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:P1000015_-_panoramio.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/P1000015_-_panoramio.jpg/220px-P1000015_-_panoramio.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/P1000015_-_panoramio.jpg/330px-P1000015_-_panoramio.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/P1000015_-_panoramio.jpg/440px-P1000015_-_panoramio.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:P1000015_-_panoramio.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>High-rise buildings in <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 2012, Qatar retained its title of richest country in the world (according to per capita income) for the third time in a row, having first overtaken <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> in 2010. According to the study published by the <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">Washington</a>-based Institute of International Finance, Qatar's per capita GDP at purchasing power parity (PPP) was $106,000 (QR387,000) in 2012, helping the country retain its ranking as the world's wealthiest nation. Luxembourg came a distant second with nearly $80,000 and Singapore third with per capita income of about $61,000. The research put Qatar's GDP at $182bn in 2012 and said it had climbed to an all-time high due to soaring gas exports and high oil prices. Its population stood at 1.8 million in 2012. The same study published that Qatar Investment Authority (QIA), with assets of $115bn, was ranked 12th among the richest sovereign wealth funds in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">[226]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:QatarCentralBankOffice.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/QatarCentralBankOffice.jpg/220px-QatarCentralBankOffice.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/QatarCentralBankOffice.jpg/330px-QatarCentralBankOffice.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/QatarCentralBankOffice.jpg/440px-QatarCentralBankOffice.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:QatarCentralBankOffice.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Qatar_Central_Bank" title="Qatar Central Bank">Qatar Central Bank</a>'s office in <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Established in 2005, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Investment_Authority" title="Qatar Investment Authority">Qatar Investment Authority</a> is the country's <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_wealth_fund" title="Sovereign wealth fund">sovereign wealth fund</a>, specializing in foreign investment.<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">[227]</a></sup> Due to billions of dollars in surpluses from the oil and gas industry, the Qatari government has directed investments into United States, Europe, and <a href="/wiki/Asia_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Asia Pacific">Asia Pacific</a>. As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, the holdings were valued at $100 billion in assets. <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Holding" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatar Holding">Qatar Holding</a> is the international investment arm of QIA. Since 2009, Qatar Holding has received $30–40bn a year from the state. As of 2014<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it has investments around the world in <a href="/wiki/Valentino_SpA" class="mw-redirect" title="Valentino SpA">Valentino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Printemps" title="Printemps">Printemps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harrods" title="Harrods">Harrods</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Shard" title="The Shard">The Shard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barclays_Bank" class="mw-redirect" title="Barclays Bank">Barclays Bank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris_Saint-Germain_F.C." title="Paris Saint-Germain F.C.">Paris Saint-Germain F.C.</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Group" title="Volkswagen Group">Volkswagen Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Dutch_Shell" title="Royal Dutch Shell">Royal Dutch Shell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_America" title="Bank of America">Bank of America</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tiffany_%26_Co." title="Tiffany &amp; Co.">Tiffany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Agricultural_Bank_of_China" title="Agricultural Bank of China">Agricultural Bank of China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sainsbury%27s" title="Sainsbury's">Sainsbury's</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry" title="BlackBerry">BlackBerry</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">[228]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Santander_Brasil" title="Santander Brasil">Santander Brasil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">[229]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">[230]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The country has no taxes on non-companies,<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">[231]</a></sup> but authorities have announced plans to levy taxes on junk food and luxury items. The taxes would be implemented on goods that harm the human body – for example, fast food, tobacco products, and soft drinks. The rollout of these initial taxes is believed to be due to the fall in oil prices and a deficit that the country faced in 2016. Additionally, the country has seen job cuts in 2016 from its petroleum companies and other sectors in the government.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">[232]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">[233]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Qatar" title="Energy in Qatar">Energy in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:ORYX_GTL_Plant_-_Qatar.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/ORYX_GTL_Plant_-_Qatar.jpg/220px-ORYX_GTL_Plant_-_Qatar.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/ORYX_GTL_Plant_-_Qatar.jpg/330px-ORYX_GTL_Plant_-_Qatar.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/ORYX_GTL_Plant_-_Qatar.jpg/440px-ORYX_GTL_Plant_-_Qatar.jpg 2x" data-file-width="977" data-file-height="652"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:ORYX_GTL_Plant_-_Qatar.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Oryx <a href="/wiki/Gas_to_liquids" title="Gas to liquids">GTL</a> plant in Qatar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As of 2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Qatar&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, Qatar has proven oil reserves of 15 billion barrels and gas fields that account for more than 13% of the global resource. As a result, it is the richest state per-capita in the world. None of its 2 million residents live below the poverty line and less than 1% are unemployed.<sup id="cite_ref-bdlive.co.za_234-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdlive.co.za-234">[234]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar's economy was in a downturn from 1982 to 1989. OPEC quotas on crude oil production, the <a href="/wiki/1980s_oil_glut" title="1980s oil glut">lower price for oil</a>, and the generally unpromising outlook on international markets reduced oil earnings. In turn, the Qatari government's spending plans had to be cut to match lower income. The resulting recessionary local business climate caused many firms to lay off expatriate staff. With the economy recovering in the 1990s, expatriate populations, particularly from <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> and South Asia, have grown again. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Qatar_Export_Treemap.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Qatar_Export_Treemap.png/220px-Qatar_Export_Treemap.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Qatar_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Qatar_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Qatar_Export_Treemap.png/440px-Qatar_Export_Treemap.png 2x" data-file-width="852" data-file-height="667"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Qatar_Export_Treemap.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Graphical depiction of Qatar's product exports in 28 color-coded categories (2011).
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Oil production will not remain at the peak level of 500,000 barrels (80,000 m<sup>3</sup>) per day for long as the national oil fields are projected to be largely depleted by 2023. Large natural gas reserves have, however, been located off Qatar's northeast coast. Qatar's proved reserves of gas are the third-largest in the world, exceeding 250 trillion cubic feet (7,000&nbsp;km<sup>3</sup>). The economy was boosted in 1991 by completion of the $1.5-billion Phase I of North Field gas development. In 1996, the Qatargas project began exporting <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas" title="Liquefied natural gas">liquefied natural gas</a> (LNG) to Japan. Further phases of North Field gas development costing billions of dollars are in various stages of planning and development. </p>
      <p>Qatar's heavy industrial projects, all based in <a href="/wiki/Umm_Said" class="mw-redirect" title="Umm Said">Umm Said</a>, include a refinery with a 50,000 barrels (8,000 m<sup>3</sup>) per day capacity, a fertiliser plant for urea and ammonia, a steel plant, and a petrochemical plant. All these industries use gas for fuel. Most are joint ventures between European and Japanese firms and the state-owned <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Petroleum" title="Qatar Petroleum">Qatar General Petroleum Corporation</a> (QGPC). The US is the major equipment supplier for Qatar's oil and gas industry, and US companies are playing a major role in North Field gas development.<sup id="cite_ref-bdlive.co.za_234-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdlive.co.za-234">[234]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar's <a href="/wiki/Qatar_National_Vision_2030" title="Qatar National Vision 2030">National Vision 2030</a> has made investment in renewable resources a major goal for the country over the next two decades.<sup id="cite_ref-Qatar_National_Vision_2030_215-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Qatar_National_Vision_2030-215">[215]</a></sup> Qatar pursues a vigorous programme of "<a href="/wiki/Qatarization" title="Qatarization">Qatarisation</a>", under which all joint venture industries and government departments strive to move Qatari nationals into positions of greater authority. Growing numbers of foreign-educated Qataris, including many educated in the US, are returning home to assume key positions formerly occupied by expatriates. To control the influx of expatriate workers, Qatar has tightened the administration of its foreign manpower programmes over the past several years. Security is the principal basis for Qatar's strict entry and immigration rules and regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-bdlive.co.za_234-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bdlive.co.za-234">[234]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Qatar" title="Transport in Qatar">Transport in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Hamad_International_Airport_Doha_Qatar_6.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Hamad_International_Airport_Doha_Qatar_6.jpg/220px-Hamad_International_Airport_Doha_Qatar_6.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Hamad_International_Airport_Doha_Qatar_6.jpg/330px-Hamad_International_Airport_Doha_Qatar_6.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Hamad_International_Airport_Doha_Qatar_6.jpg/440px-Hamad_International_Airport_Doha_Qatar_6.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Hamad_International_Airport_Doha_Qatar_6.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hamad_International_Airport" title="Hamad International Airport">Hamad International Airport</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>With a fast-expanding population and substantial economic growth over the past decade, a reliable and extensive transportation network is becoming increasingly necessary within Qatar. So far the government, the primary transport developer, has done well in terms of keeping up with the demand for new transportation options. In 2008 the <a href="/wiki/Ashghal" title="Ashghal">Public Works Authority</a> (Ashghal), one of the bodies that oversees infrastructure development, underwent a major reorganisation in order to streamline and modernise the authority in preparation for major project expansions across all segments in the near future. Ashghal works in tandem with the Urban Planning and Development Authority (UPDA), the body that designed the transportation master plan, instituted in March 2006 and running to 2025. </p>
      <p>As driving is the primary mode of transport in Qatar, the road network is a major focus of the plan. Project highlights in this segment include the multibillion-dollar Doha Expressway and the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Bahrain_Causeway" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatar Bahrain Causeway">Qatar Bahrain Causeway</a>, which will connect Qatar to Bahrain and Saudi Arabia and is considered a milestone in regional interconnectivity. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:QTR_A7-APA_A380!137_EDHI_16-04-14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/QTR_A7-APA_A380%21137_EDHI_16-04-14.jpg/220px-QTR_A7-APA_A380%21137_EDHI_16-04-14.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/QTR_A7-APA_A380%21137_EDHI_16-04-14.jpg/330px-QTR_A7-APA_A380%21137_EDHI_16-04-14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/QTR_A7-APA_A380%21137_EDHI_16-04-14.jpg/440px-QTR_A7-APA_A380%21137_EDHI_16-04-14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:QTR_A7-APA_A380!137_EDHI_16-04-14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>, Qatar Airways, one of the world's largest airlines, links over 150 international destinations from its base in <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Mass-transit options, such as a <a href="/wiki/Doha_metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Doha metro">Doha metro</a>, light-rail system and more extensive bus networks, are also under development to ease road congestion. In addition, the railway system is being significantly expanded and could eventually form an integral part of a GCC-wide network linking all the <a href="/wiki/Arab_states_of_the_Persian_Gulf" title="Arab states of the Persian Gulf">Arab states of the Persian Gulf</a>. The airport, too, is expanding capacity to keep up with rising visitor numbers. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hamad_International_Airport" title="Hamad International Airport">Hamad International Airport</a> is the <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> of <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>. In 2014, it replaced the former <a href="/wiki/Doha_International_Airport" title="Doha International Airport">Doha International Airport</a> as Qatar's principal airport. In 2016, the airport was named the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_by_passenger_traffic" title="List of busiest airports by passenger traffic">50th busiest airport in the world by passenger traffic</a>, serving 37,283,987 passengers, a 20.2% increase from 2015. </p>
      <p>Qatar is increasingly activating its logistics and ports in order to participate in trade between Europe and China or Africa. For this purpose, ports such as Hamad Port are rapidly expanded and investments are made in their technology. The country is historically and currently part of the Maritime <a href="/wiki/Silk_Road" title="Silk Road">Silk Road</a> that runs from the Chinese coast to the south via the southern tip of <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> to <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, from there through the Red Sea via the <a href="/wiki/Suez_Canal" title="Suez Canal">Suez Canal</a> to the Mediterranean, there to the Upper Adriatic region to the northern Italian hub of <a href="/wiki/Trieste" title="Trieste">Trieste</a> with its rail connections to <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">Central Europe</a>, Eastern Europe and the <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">North Sea</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">[235]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">[236]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">[237]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Hamad_Port" title="Hamad Port">Hamad Port</a> is Qatar's main seaport, located south of <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Umm_Al_Houl" title="Umm Al Houl">Umm Al Houl</a> area. Construction of the port began in 2010; it became operational in December 2016. It was officially opened in September 2017, and is expected to become fully operational by 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">[238]</a></sup> Capable of handling up to 7.8 million tonnes of products annually, the bulk of trade which passes through the port consists of food and building materials.<sup id="cite_ref-reuters1_239-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reuters1-239">[239]</a></sup> On the northern coast, <a href="/wiki/Ras_Laffan_Industrial_City#Port_of_Ras_Laffan" title="Ras Laffan Industrial City">Ras Laffan Port</a> serves as the most extensive LNG exporting facility in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">[240]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> is one of the <a href="/wiki/World%27s_largest_airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="World's largest airlines">largest airlines in the world</a> that serves in six continents connecting more than 160 destinations every day. Besides, it has won Airline of the Year in 2011, 2012, 2015, 2017 and 2019 due to its outstanding performance and employs more than 46,000 professionals.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">[241]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">[242]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Qatar" title="Demographics of Qatar">Demographics of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;overflow:hidden;width:auto;max-width:1008px">
       <div class="thumbinner">
        <div class="noresize" style="overflow:auto">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Doha_skyline_banner.jpg" class="image" title="Skyline of Doha, capital and largest city of Qatar"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Doha_skyline_banner.jpg/1000px-Doha_skyline_banner.jpg" decoding="async" width="1000" height="143" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Doha_skyline_banner.jpg/1500px-Doha_skyline_banner.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/Doha_skyline_banner.jpg/2000px-Doha_skyline_banner.jpg 2x" data-file-width="9225" data-file-height="1317"></a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:The_Doha_city_skyline,_featuring_post-modern_structures,_view_from_Al_Corniche.jpg" title="File:The Doha city skyline, featuring post-modern structures, view from Al Corniche.jpg"> </a>
