      <p>The number of people in Qatar fluctuates considerably depending on the season, since the country relies heavily on migrant labour. In early 2017, Qatar's total population was 2.6 million, with foreigners making up a vast majority of Qatar's population. Only 313,000 of the population (12%) were Qatari citizens, while the remaining 2.3 million (88%) were <a href="/wiki/Expatriates" class="mw-redirect" title="Expatriates">expatriates</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pop_19-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-19">[19]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The combined number of <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asians</a> (from the countries of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_subcontinent" title="Indian subcontinent">Indian subcontinent</a> including Sri Lanka) by themselves represent over 1.5 million people (60%) of Qatar's population. Among these, <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Qatar" title="Indians in Qatar">Indians</a> are the largest community, numbering 650,000 in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-pop_19-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-19">[19]</a></sup> followed by 350,000 <a href="/wiki/Nepalis_in_Qatar" title="Nepalis in Qatar">Nepalis</a>, 280,000 <a href="/wiki/Bangladeshis" title="Bangladeshis">Bangladeshis</a>, 145,000 <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lankans" class="mw-redirect" title="Sri Lankans">Sri Lankans</a>, and 125,000 <a href="/wiki/Pakistanis_in_Qatar" title="Pakistanis in Qatar">Pakistanis</a>. The contingent of expatriates which are not of South Asian origin represent around 28% of Qatar's population, of which the largest group is 260,000 <a href="/wiki/Filipinos_in_Qatar" title="Filipinos in Qatar">Filipinos</a> and 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptians</a>, plus many other nationalities (including nationals of other Arab countries, Europeans, etc.).<sup id="cite_ref-pop_19-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pop-19">[19]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pearl-Qatar_Doha_Qatar_11Nov2017_SkySat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Pearl-Qatar_Doha_Qatar_11Nov2017_SkySat.jpg/220px-Pearl-Qatar_Doha_Qatar_11Nov2017_SkySat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Pearl-Qatar_Doha_Qatar_11Nov2017_SkySat.jpg/330px-Pearl-Qatar_Doha_Qatar_11Nov2017_SkySat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Pearl-Qatar_Doha_Qatar_11Nov2017_SkySat.jpg/440px-Pearl-Qatar_Doha_Qatar_11Nov2017_SkySat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="700"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pearl-Qatar_Doha_Qatar_11Nov2017_SkySat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Residential buildings at <a href="/wiki/The_Pearl-Qatar" title="The Pearl-Qatar">the Pearl</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Qatar's first demographic records date back to 1892, and were conducted by Ottoman governors in the region. Based on this census, which includes only the residents in cities, the total population in 1892 was 9,830.<sup id="cite_ref-Fromhertz2012_73-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fromhertz2012-73">[73]</a></sup> The 2010 census recorded the total population at 1,699,435.<sup id="cite_ref-census10_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census10-5">[5]</a></sup> In January 2013, the Qatar Statistics Authority estimated the country's population at 1,903,447, of which 1,405,164 were males and 498,283 females.<sup id="cite_ref-qsa-jan13_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qsa-jan13-245">[245]</a></sup> At the time of the first census, held in 1970, the population was 111,133.<sup id="cite_ref-qsahist_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qsahist-246">[246]</a></sup> The population has tripled in the decade to 2011, up from just over 600,000 people in 2001, leaving Qatari nationals as less than 15% of the total population.<sup id="cite_ref-balancing_247-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-balancing-247">[247]</a></sup> The influx of male labourers has skewed the gender balance, and women are now just one-quarter of the population. </p>
      <p>Projections released by the Qatar Statistical Authority indicate that the total population of Qatar could reach 2.8 million by 2020. Qatar's National Development Strategy (2011–16) had estimated that the country's population would reach 1.78m in 2013, 1.81m in 2014, 1.84m in 2015 and 1.86m in 2016 – the yearly growth rate being merely 2.1%. But the country's population has soared to 1.83 million by the end of 2012, showing 7.5% growth over the previous year.<sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">[248]</a></sup> Qatar's total population hit a record high of 2.46 million in November 2015, an increase of 8.5% from the previous year, far exceeding official projections.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">[249]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Qatar" title="Religion in Qatar">Religion in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Alwakhra_Masjid.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Alwakhra_Masjid.jpg/220px-Alwakhra_Masjid.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Alwakhra_Masjid.jpg/330px-Alwakhra_Masjid.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Alwakhra_Masjid.jpg/440px-Alwakhra_Masjid.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2754" data-file-height="1958"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Alwakhra_Masjid.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Mosque in Qatar
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a> is Qatar's predominant religion and is the <a href="/wiki/State_religion" title="State religion">official status</a> although not the only religion practiced in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">[250]</a></sup> Most Qatari citizens belong to the <a href="/wiki/Salafi" class="mw-redirect" title="Salafi">Salafi</a> <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a> movement of <a href="/wiki/Wahhabism" title="Wahhabism">Wahhabism</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-wahh_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wahh-251">[251]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-insom_252-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insom-252">[252]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-risingreuters_253-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-risingreuters-253">[253]</a></sup> and between 5–15% of Muslims in Qatar follow <a href="/wiki/Shia_Islam" title="Shia Islam">Shia Islam</a> with other Muslims sects being very small in number.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> In 2010, Qatar's population was 67.7% <a href="/wiki/Muslim" class="mw-redirect" title="Muslim">Muslim</a>, 13.8% <a href="/wiki/Christians" title="Christians">Christian</a>, 13.8% <a href="/wiki/Hindu" class="mw-redirect" title="Hindu">Hindu</a>, and 3.1% <a href="/wiki/Buddhist" class="mw-redirect" title="Buddhist">Buddhist</a>; other religions and religiously unaffiliated people accounted for the remaining 1.6%.<sup id="cite_ref-pewrel_255-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pewrel-255">[255]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sharia_law" class="mw-redirect" title="Sharia law">Sharia law</a> is the main source of Qatari legislation according to Qatar's Constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-con_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-con-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qat1_115-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qat1-115">[115]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The vision of the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Awqaf_and_Islamic_Affairs_(Qatar)" title="Ministry of Awqaf and Islamic Affairs (Qatar)">Ministry of Awqaf and Islamic Affairs (Qatar)</a> is "to build a contemporary Islamic society along with fostering the <a href="/wiki/Sharia" title="Sharia">Sharee’ah</a> and cultural heritage".<sup id="cite_ref-Contempory_Sharee’ah_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Contempory_Sharee’ah-256">[256]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Qatar" title="Christianity in Qatar">Christian population</a> is composed almost entirely of foreigners. Since 2008, Christians have been allowed to build churches on ground donated by the government,<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">[257]</a></sup> though foreign missionary activity is officially discouraged.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">[258]</a></sup> Active churches include the <a href="/wiki/Malankara_Mar_Thoma_Syrian_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Malankara Mar Thoma Syrian Church">Mar Thoma Church</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malankara_Orthodox_Syrian_Church" title="Malankara Orthodox Syrian Church">Malankara Orthodox Syrian Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church_of_Our_Lady_of_the_Rosary_(Doha)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catholic Church of Our Lady of the Rosary (Doha)">Church of Our Lady of the Rosary</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Anglican" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican">Anglican</a> Church of the Epiphany.<sup id="cite_ref-Report_on_Qatar_259-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Report_on_Qatar-259">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Anglican_Centre_in_Qatar_260-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Anglican_Centre_in_Qatar-260">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_University_Press_261-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_University_Press-261">[261]</a></sup> There are also two <a href="/wiki/Ward_(LDS_Church)" title="Ward (LDS Church)">Mormon wards</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Report_on_Qatar_259-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Report_on_Qatar-259">[259]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-The_Anglican_Centre_in_Qatar_260-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Anglican_Centre_in_Qatar-260">[260]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Oxford_University_Press_261-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oxford_University_Press-261">[261]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span></h3> 
      <p>Arabic is the official language of Qatar, with <a href="/wiki/Qatari_Arabic" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatari Arabic">Qatari Arabic</a> the local dialect. <a href="/wiki/Qatari_Sign_Language" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatari Sign Language">Qatari Sign Language</a> is the language of the deaf community. <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is commonly used as a second language,<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">[262]</a></sup> and a rising <a href="/wiki/Lingua_franca" title="Lingua franca">lingua franca</a>, especially in commerce, to the extent that steps are being taken to try to preserve Arabic from English's encroachment.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">[263]</a></sup> English is particularly useful for communication with Qatar's large expatriate community. In the medical community, and in situations such as the training of nurses to work in Qatar, English acts as a lingua franca.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">[264]</a></sup> Reflecting the multicultural make-up of the country, many other languages are also spoken, including <a href="/wiki/Persian_language" title="Persian language">Persian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baluchi_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Baluchi language">Baluchi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brahui_language" title="Brahui language">Brahui</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hindi" title="Hindi">Hindi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">Malayalam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Urdu" title="Urdu">Urdu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pashto" title="Pashto">Pashto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kannada_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Kannada language">Kannada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Telugu_language" title="Telugu language">Telugu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nepali_language" title="Nepali language">Nepali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sinhalese_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Sinhalese language">Sinhalese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bengali_language" title="Bengali language">Bengali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">[265]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2012, Qatar joined the international French-speaking organisation of <a href="/wiki/Organisation_internationale_de_la_Francophonie" title="Organisation internationale de la Francophonie">La Francophonie</a> (OIF) as a new associate member, but in December 2013, the French daily <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i> revealed that Qatar, which has very few native French speakers, had not yet paid any contribution to the OIF,<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">[266]</a></sup> while the outgoing Administrator of the OIF complained in 2015 that Qatar had not kept any of the promises it made when it joined the organisation and had never paid its annual membership fees.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">[267]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Qatar" title="Culture of Qatar">Culture of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_festivals_in_Qatar" title="List of festivals in Qatar">List of festivals in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Qatar's culture is similar to other countries in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Arabia" title="Eastern Arabia">Eastern Arabia</a>, being significantly influenced by Islam. <a href="/wiki/Qatar_National_Day" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatar National Day">Qatar National Day</a>, hosted annually on 18 December, has had an important role in developing a sense of national identity.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">[268]</a></sup> It is observed in remembrance of <a href="/wiki/Jassim_bin_Mohammed_Al_Thani" title="Jassim bin Mohammed Al Thani">Jassim bin Mohammed Al Thani</a>'s succession to the throne and his subsequent unification of the country's various tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">[269]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">[270]</a></sup> Since 1 July 2008, <a href="/wiki/Hamad_Bin_Abdulaziz_Al-Kawari" title="Hamad Bin Abdulaziz Al-Kawari">Hamad Bin Abdulaziz Al-Kawari</a> has been the Minister for Culture, Arts and Heritage of Qatar. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Arts_and_museums">Arts and museums</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Collecting_practices_of_the_Al-Thani_Family" title="Collecting practices of the Al-Thani Family">Collecting practices of the Al-Thani Family</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qatari_art" title="Qatari art">Qatari art</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Public_art_in_Qatar" title="Public art in Qatar">Public art in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:IslamicArtMuseumDohaSkyline.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/IslamicArtMuseumDohaSkyline.jpg/220px-IslamicArtMuseumDohaSkyline.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/IslamicArtMuseumDohaSkyline.jpg/330px-IslamicArtMuseumDohaSkyline.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/IslamicArtMuseumDohaSkyline.jpg/440px-IslamicArtMuseumDohaSkyline.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="675"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:IslamicArtMuseumDohaSkyline.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Islamic_Art,_Doha" title="Museum of Islamic Art, Doha">Museum of Islamic Art</a> in Doha
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Several senior members of Qatar's ruling Al Thani family are noted collectors of Islamic and contemporary art. </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Islamic_Art,_Doha" title="Museum of Islamic Art, Doha">Museum of Islamic Art</a>, opened in 2008, is regarded as one of the best museums in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-sandsmith_271-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sandsmith-271">[271]</a></sup> This, and several other Qatari museums, like the <a href="/wiki/Mathaf:_Arab_Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Mathaf: Arab Museum of Modern Art">Arab Museum of Modern Art</a>, falls under the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Museums_Authority" title="Qatar Museums Authority">Qatar Museums Authority</a> (<i>QMA</i>) which is led by Sheikha <a href="/wiki/Al-Mayassa_bint_Hamad_bin_Khalifa_Al-Thani" title="Al-Mayassa bint Hamad bin Khalifa Al-Thani">Al-Mayassa bint Hamad bin Khalifa Al-Thani</a>, the sister of the ruling Emir of the State of Qatar, and the prominent collector and art patron Sheikh <a href="/wiki/Hassan_bin_Mohamed_bin_Ali_Al_Thani" title="Hassan bin Mohamed bin Ali Al Thani">Hassan bin Mohammed Al Thani</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">[272]</a></sup> The QMA also sponsors artistic events abroad, such as major exhibitions by Takahashi Murakami in Versailles (2010) and Damien Hirst in London (2012). </p>
      <p>Qatar is the world's biggest buyer in the art market by value.<sup id="cite_ref-theart_273-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theart-273">[273]</a></sup> The Qatari cultural sector is being developed to enable the country to reach world recognition to contribute to the development of a country that comes mainly from its resources from the gas industry.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">[274]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Museum_of_Qatar" title="National Museum of Qatar">National Museum of Qatar</a> was opened to the public on 28 March 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">[275]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Qatari_literature" title="Qatari literature">Qatari literature</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Sign_for_Oxygen_Park_in_Education_City.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sign_for_Oxygen_Park_in_Education_City.jpg/220px-Sign_for_Oxygen_Park_in_Education_City.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sign_for_Oxygen_Park_in_Education_City.jpg/330px-Sign_for_Oxygen_Park_in_Education_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Sign_for_Oxygen_Park_in_Education_City.jpg/440px-Sign_for_Oxygen_Park_in_Education_City.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5984" data-file-height="3366"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sign_for_Oxygen_Park_in_Education_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Qatar_National_Library" title="Qatar National Library">Qatar National Library</a> in Doha
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Qatari literature traces its origins back to the 19th century. Originally, written <a href="/wiki/Poetry" title="Poetry">poetry</a> was the most common form of expression. Abdul Jalil Al-Tabatabai and Mohammed bin Abdullah bin Uthaymeen, two poets dating back to the early 19th century, formed the corpus of Qatar's earliest written poetry. Poetry later fell out of favor after Qatar began reaping the profits from oil exports in the mid-20th century and many Qataris abandoned their <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> traditions in favor of more urban lifestyles.<sup id="cite_ref-tawfiq_276-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tawfiq-276">[276]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Due to the increasing number of Qataris who began receiving formal education during the 1950s and other significant societal changes, 1970 witnessed the introduction of the first <a href="/wiki/Short_story" title="Short story">short story</a> anthology, and in 1993 the first locally authored <a href="/wiki/Novel" title="Novel">novels</a> were published. Poetry, particularly the predominant <a href="/wiki/Nabati" title="Nabati">nabati</a> form, retained some importance but would soon be overshadowed by other literary types.<sup id="cite_ref-tawfiq_276-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tawfiq-276">[276]</a></sup> Unlike most other forms of art in Qatari society, females have been involved in the modern literature movement on a similar magnitude to males.<sup id="cite_ref-cambridge1_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cambridge1-277">[277]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Media_of_Qatar" class="mw-redirect" title="Media of Qatar">Media of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Al_Jazeera_English_Newsdesk.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Al_Jazeera_English_Newsdesk.jpg/220px-Al_Jazeera_English_Newsdesk.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Al_Jazeera_English_Newsdesk.jpg/330px-Al_Jazeera_English_Newsdesk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Al_Jazeera_English_Newsdesk.jpg/440px-Al_Jazeera_English_Newsdesk.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Al_Jazeera_English_Newsdesk.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The news desk of <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_English" title="Al Jazeera English">Al Jazeera English</a>, a Qatari news channel
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Qatar's media was classified as "not free" in the 2014 <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_the_Press_(report)" title="Freedom of the Press (report)">Freedom of the Press</a> report by <a href="/wiki/Freedom_House" title="Freedom House">Freedom House</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse1_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse1-278">[278]</a></sup> TV broadcasting in Qatar was started in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">[279]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera" title="Al Jazeera">Al Jazeera</a> is a main television network headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Doha" title="Doha">Doha</a>, Qatar. Al Jazeera initially launched in 1996 as an <a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> news and current affairs <a href="/wiki/Satellite" title="Satellite">satellite</a> TV channel of the same name, but has since expanded into a global network of several speciality TV&nbsp;channels known collectively as the <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Media_Network" title="Al Jazeera Media Network">Al Jazeera Media Network</a>. </p>
      <p>It has been reported that journalists practice <a href="/wiki/Self-censorship" title="Self-censorship">self-censorship</a>, particularly in regards to the government and <a href="/wiki/House_of_Thani" class="mw-redirect" title="House of Thani">ruling family</a> of Qatar.<sup id="cite_ref-blanchard_280-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blanchard-280">[280]</a></sup> Criticism of the government, Emir and ruling family in the media is illegal. According to article 46 of the press law "The Emir of the state of Qatar shall not be criticised and no statement can be attributed to him unless under a written permission from the manager of his office."<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">[281]</a></sup> Journalists are also subject to prosecution for insulting <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-freedomhouse1_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freedomhouse1-278">[278]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2014, a <a href="/wiki/Computer_crime" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer crime">Cybercrime</a> Prevention Law was passed. The law is said to restrict press freedom and carries prison sentences and fines for broad reasons such as jeopardising local peace or publishing false news.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">[282]</a></sup> The Gulf Center for Human Rights has stated that the law is a threat to freedom of speech and has called for certain articles of the law to be revoked.<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">[283]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Press media has undergone expansion in recent years. There are currently <a href="/wiki/List_of_newspapers_in_Qatar" title="List of newspapers in Qatar">seven newspapers in circulation in Qatar</a>, with four being published in Arabic and three being published in English.<sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">[284]</a></sup> There are also newspapers from India, Nepal and Sri Lanka with editions printed from Qatar. </p>
      <p>In regards to telecommunication infrastructure, Qatar is the highest-ranked Middle Eastern country in the World Economic Forum's Network Readiness Index (NRI) – an indicator for determining the development level of a country's information and communication technologies. Qatar ranked number 23 overall in the 2014 NRI ranking, unchanged from 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">[285]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Qatar" title="Music of Qatar">Music of Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The music of Qatar is based on <a href="/wiki/Bedouin" title="Bedouin">Bedouin</a> poetry, song and dance. Traditional dances in Doha are performed on Friday afternoons; one such dance is the <a href="/wiki/Ardah" title="Ardah">Ardah</a>, a stylised martial dance performed by two rows of dancers who are accompanied by an array of <a href="/wiki/Percussion_instrument" title="Percussion instrument">percussion instruments</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Al-ras_(drum)" title="Al-ras (drum)">al-ras</a> (a large drum whose leather is heated by an open fire), <a href="/wiki/Tambourine" title="Tambourine">tambourines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cymbal" title="Cymbal">cymbals</a> with small drums.<sup id="cite_ref-qatarembassy1_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qatarembassy1-286">[286]</a></sup> Other percussion instruments used in folk music include <i>galahs</i> (a tall clay jar) and tin drinking cups known as <i>tus</i> or <i>tasat</i>, usually used in conjunction with a <i>tabl</i>, a longitudinal drum beaten with a stick.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">[287]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/String_instrument" title="String instrument">String instruments</a>, such as the <a href="/wiki/Oud" title="Oud">oud</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rebaba" class="mw-redirect" title="Rebaba">rebaba</a>, are also commonly used.<sup id="cite_ref-qatarembassy1_286-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qatarembassy1-286">[286]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Qatar" title="Sport in Qatar">Sport in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar_Cucinotta_winning_stage_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar_Cucinotta_winning_stage_1.jpg/220px-2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar_Cucinotta_winning_stage_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar_Cucinotta_winning_stage_1.jpg/330px-2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar_Cucinotta_winning_stage_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar_Cucinotta_winning_stage_1.jpg/440px-2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar_Cucinotta_winning_stage_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="576"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar_Cucinotta_winning_stage_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/2015_Ladies_Tour_of_Qatar" title="2015 Ladies Tour of Qatar">2015 Ladies Tour of Qatar</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Association football</a> is the most popular sport in Qatar, both in terms of players and spectators.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">[288]</a></sup> Shortly after the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Football_Association" title="Qatar Football Association">Qatar Football Association</a> became affiliated with <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a> in 1970, one of the country's earliest international accolades came in 1981 when the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_national_under-20_football_team" title="Qatar national under-20 football team">Qatar national under-20 team</a>'s emerged as runners-up to West Germany in that year's <a href="/wiki/1981_FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" title="1981 FIFA World Youth Championship">edition</a> of the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Youth_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="FIFA World Youth Championship">FIFA World Youth Championship</a> after being defeated 4–0 in the final. At the senior level, Qatar has played host to two editions of the <a href="/wiki/AFC_Asian_Cup" title="AFC Asian Cup">AFC Asian Cup</a>; the first coming being the 9th edition in <a href="/wiki/1988_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="1988 AFC Asian Cup">1988</a> and the second being the 15th edition held in <a href="/wiki/2011_AFC_Asian_Cup" title="2011 AFC Asian Cup">2011</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">[289]</a></sup> For the first time in the country's history, the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_national_football_team" title="Qatar national football team">Qatar national football team</a> won the AFC Asian Cup in the <a href="/wiki/2019_Asian_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="2019 Asian Cup">2019 edition</a> hosted in the UAE, beating <a href="/wiki/Japan_national_football_team" title="Japan national football team">Japan</a> 3–1 in the final. They won all seven of their matches, conceding only a single goal throughout the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">[290]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 2 December 2010, Qatar won their bid to host the <a href="/wiki/2022_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2022 FIFA World Cup">2022 FIFA World Cup</a>, despite never previously qualifying for the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup_Finals" class="mw-redirect" title="FIFA World Cup Finals">FIFA World Cup Finals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">[291]</a></sup> Local organisers are planning to build 9 new stadiums and expand 3 existing stadiums for this event. Qatar's winning bid for the 2022 World Cup was greeted enthusiastically in the Persian Gulf region as it was the first time a country in the Middle East had been selected to host the tournament. However, the bid has been embroiled in much controversy, including allegations of bribery and interference in the investigation of the alleged bribery. European football associations have also objected to the 2022 World Cup being held in Qatar for a variety of reasons, from the impact of warm temperatures on players' fitness, to the disruption it might cause in European domestic league calendars should the event be rescheduled to take place during winter.<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">[292]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">[293]</a></sup> In May 2014, Qatari football official <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_bin_Hammam" title="Mohammed bin Hammam">Mohammed bin Hammam</a> was accused of making payments totalling £3m to officials in return for their support for the Qatar bid.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">[294]</a></sup> However, a FIFA inquiry into the bidding process in November 2014 cleared Qatar of any wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">[295]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:2009_Emir_of_Qatar_Cup_Final_-_DSC_0518_(3581777008).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/2009_Emir_of_Qatar_Cup_Final_-_DSC_0518_%283581777008%29.jpg/220px-2009_Emir_of_Qatar_Cup_Final_-_DSC_0518_%283581777008%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/2009_Emir_of_Qatar_Cup_Final_-_DSC_0518_%283581777008%29.jpg/330px-2009_Emir_of_Qatar_Cup_Final_-_DSC_0518_%283581777008%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/2009_Emir_of_Qatar_Cup_Final_-_DSC_0518_%283581777008%29.jpg/440px-2009_Emir_of_Qatar_Cup_Final_-_DSC_0518_%283581777008%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2896" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:2009_Emir_of_Qatar_Cup_Final_-_DSC_0518_(3581777008).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Qatar_Emir_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatar Emir Cup">Qatar Emir Cup</a> in 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>, a British national daily newspaper, produced a short documentary named "Abuse and exploitation of migrant workers preparing emirate for 2022".<sup id="cite_ref-Guardian20130925_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian20130925-296">[296]</a></sup> A 2014 investigation by <i>The Guardian</i> reports that migrant workers who have been constructing luxurious offices for the organisers of the 2022 World Cup have not been paid in over a year, and are now "working illegally from cockroach-infested lodgings."<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">[297]</a></sup> For 2014, Nepalese migrants involved in constructing infrastructure for the 2022 World Cup died at a rate of one every two days.<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">[298]</a></sup> The Qatar 2022 organising committee have responded to various allegations by claiming that hosting the World Cup in Qatar would act as a "catalyst for change" in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">[299]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Qatar was estimated to host a <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">football</a> fan base of 1.6 million for the <a href="/wiki/World_Cup_2022" class="mw-redirect" title="World Cup 2022">World Cup 2022</a>. However, the construction work in country was expected to only take the available 37,000 hotel rooms to 70,000 by the end of 2021. In December 2019, the Qatari World Cup officials approached the <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">Glastonbury Festival</a> chiefs and the organizers of the <a href="/wiki/Coachella_Valley_Music_and_Arts_Festival" title="Coachella Valley Music and Arts Festival">Coachella festival</a> to plan huge desert campsites for thousands of football fans. The World Cup campsites on the outskirts were reported to have licensed bars, restaurants, entertainment and washing facilities. Moreover, two cruise ships were also reserved as temporary floating accommodations for nearly 40,000 people during the tournament.<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">[300]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Though football is the most popular sport, other team sports have experienced considerable success at senior level. In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_men%27s_national_handball_team" title="Qatar men's national handball team">national handball team</a> emerged as runners-up to <a href="/wiki/France_men%27s_national_handball_team" title="France men's national handball team">France</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Men%27s_Handball_Championship" title="2015 World Men's Handball Championship">World Men's Handball Championship</a> as hosts, however the tournament was marred by numerous controversies regarding the host nation and its team.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">[301]</a></sup> Further, in 2014, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_national_3x3_team" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatar national 3x3 team">Qatar</a> won the world championship in men's <a href="/wiki/FIBA_3x3_World_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="FIBA 3x3 World Championships">3x3 basketball</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">[302]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Khalifa_International_Tennis_and_Squash_Complex" title="Khalifa International Tennis and Squash Complex">Khalifa International Tennis and Squash Complex</a> in Doha hosted the <a href="/wiki/WTA_Tour_Championships" class="mw-redirect" title="WTA Tour Championships">WTA Tour Championships</a> in women's tennis between 2008 and 2010. Doha holds the <a href="/wiki/Women%27s_Tennis_Association" title="Women's Tennis Association">WTA</a> Premier tournament <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Ladies_Open" class="mw-redirect" title="Qatar Ladies Open">Qatar Ladies Open</a> annually. Since 2002, Qatar has hosted the annual <a href="/wiki/Tour_of_Qatar" title="Tour of Qatar">Tour of Qatar</a>, a cycling race in six stages. Every February, riders are racing on the roads across Qatar's flat land for six days. Each stage covers a distance of more than 100&nbsp;km, though the time trial usually is a shorter distance. Tour of Qatar is organised by the Qatar Cycling Federation for professional riders in the category of Elite Men.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">[303]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Qatar Army Skydiving Team has several different skydiving disciplines placing among the top nations in the world. The Qatar National Parachute team performs annually during Qatar's National Day and at other large events, such as the 2015 World Handball Championship.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">[304]</a></sup> Doha four times was the host of the official <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Men%27s_Club_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Men's Club World Championship">FIVB Volleyball Men's Club World Championship</a> and three times host <a href="/wiki/FIVB_Volleyball_Women%27s_Club_World_Championship" title="FIVB Volleyball Women's Club World Championship">FIVB Volleyball Women's Club World Championship</a>. Doha one time Host <a href="/wiki/1997_Asian_Men%27s_Volleyball_Championship" title="1997 Asian Men's Volleyball Championship">Asian Volleyball Championship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">[305]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 3 September 2020, the <a href="/wiki/Education_City_Stadium" title="Education City Stadium">Education City Stadium</a>, hosted its first match ever official match, where the local clubs <a href="/wiki/Al_Sadd_SC" title="Al Sadd SC">Al Sadd SC</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al_Kharaitiyat_SC" title="Al Kharaitiyat SC">Al Kharaitiyat SC</a> contested the season-opener of 2020-21 <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Stars_League" title="Qatar Stars League">Qatar Stars League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">[306]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Qatar" title="Education in Qatar">Education in Qatar</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_Student_Center_in_Education_City.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Entrance_to_Student_Center_in_Education_City.jpg/220px-Entrance_to_Student_Center_in_Education_City.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Entrance_to_Student_Center_in_Education_City.jpg/330px-Entrance_to_Student_Center_in_Education_City.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Entrance_to_Student_Center_in_Education_City.jpg/440px-Entrance_to_Student_Center_in_Education_City.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1634" data-file-height="1087"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Entrance_to_Student_Center_in_Education_City.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Student Center in <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City</a>. Education City houses various educational facilities, including satellite campuses of eight international universities.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Qatar hired the <a href="/wiki/RAND_Corporation" title="RAND Corporation">RAND Corporation</a> to reform its K–12 education system.<sup id="cite_ref-strangepow_179-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strangepow-179">[179]</a></sup> Through <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Foundation" title="Qatar Foundation">Qatar Foundation</a>, the country has built <a href="/wiki/Education_City" title="Education City">Education City</a>, a campus which hosts local branches of the <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_College_in_Qatar" title="Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar">Weill Cornell Medical College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carnegie_Mellon_School_of_Computer_Science" title="Carnegie Mellon School of Computer Science">Carnegie Mellon School of Computer Science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University_School_of_Foreign_Service_in_Qatar" class="mw-redirect" title="Georgetown University School of Foreign Service in Qatar">Georgetown University School of Foreign Service</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northwestern_University_in_Qatar" title="Northwestern University in Qatar">Northwestern's Medill School of Journalism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_at_Qatar" title="Texas A&amp;M University at Qatar">Texas A&amp;M's School of Engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Commonwealth_University_-_Qatar" title="Virginia Commonwealth University - Qatar">Virginia Commonwealth University School of the Arts</a> and other Western institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-strangepow_179-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strangepow-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wapo_307-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wapo-307">[307]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_literacy_rate" title="List of countries by literacy rate">illiteracy rate</a> in Qatar was 3.1% for males and 4.2% for females in 2012, the lowest in the Arab-speaking world, but 86th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">[308]</a></sup> Citizens are required to attend government-provided education from <a href="/wiki/Kindergarten" title="Kindergarten">kindergarten</a> through high school.<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">[309]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Qatar_University" title="Qatar University">Qatar University</a>, founded in 1973, is the country's oldest and largest institution of higher education.<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">[310]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">[311]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:QatarUniversityEastView.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/QatarUniversityEastView.jpg/220px-QatarUniversityEastView.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/QatarUniversityEastView.jpg/330px-QatarUniversityEastView.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/58/QatarUniversityEastView.jpg/440px-QatarUniversityEastView.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="450"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:QatarUniversityEastView.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Qatar_University" title="Qatar University">Qatar University</a>, east view
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In November 2002, emir Hamad bin Khalifa Al Thani created <a href="/wiki/The_Supreme_Education_Council_(Qatar)" class="mw-redirect" title="The Supreme Education Council (Qatar)">The Supreme Education Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">[312]</a></sup> The Council directs and controls education for all ages from the <a href="/wiki/Nursery_school" class="mw-redirect" title="Nursery school">pre-school</a> level through the university level, including the "Education for a New Era" initiative which was established to try to position Qatar as a leader in education reform.<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">[313]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">[314]</a></sup> According to the <a href="/wiki/Webometrics_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Webometrics Ranking of World Universities">Webometrics Ranking of World Universities</a>, the top-ranking universities in the country are Qatar University (1,881st worldwide), <a href="/wiki/Texas_A%26M_University_at_Qatar" title="Texas A&amp;M University at Qatar">Texas A&amp;M University at Qatar</a> (3,905th) and <a href="/wiki/Weill_Cornell_Medical_College_in_Qatar" title="Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar">Weill Cornell Medical College in Qatar</a> (6,855th).<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">[315]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2008, Qatar established the <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Science_%26_Technology_Park" title="Qatar Science &amp; Technology Park">Qatar Science &amp; Technology Park</a> in Education City to link those universities with industry. Education City is also home to a fully <a href="/wiki/School_accreditation" class="mw-redirect" title="School accreditation">accredited</a> <a href="/wiki/International_Baccalaureate" title="International Baccalaureate">international Baccalaureate</a> school, <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Academy" title="Qatar Academy">Qatar Academy</a>. In addition, two Canadian institutions, the <a href="/wiki/College_of_the_North_Atlantic" title="College of the North Atlantic">College of the North Atlantic</a> (headquarters in Newfoundland and Labrador) and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Calgary" title="University of Calgary">University of Calgary</a>, have inaugurated campuses in Doha. Other <a href="/wiki/For-profit_school" class="mw-redirect" title="For-profit school">for-profit universities</a> have also established campuses in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">[316]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2012, Qatar was ranked third from the bottom of the 65 OECD countries participating in the PISA test of maths, reading and skills for 15- and 16-year-olds, comparable to Colombia or Albania, despite having the highest per capita income in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">[317]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">[318]</a></sup> As part of its national development strategy, Qatar has outlined a 10-year strategic plan to improve the level of education.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">[319]</a></sup> Furthermore, the government has launched educational outreach programs, such as <a href="/wiki/AL-Bairaq" class="mw-redirect" title="AL-Bairaq">Al-Bairaq</a>. Al-Bairaq was launched in 2010 aims to provide high school students with an opportunity to experience a research environment in the <a href="/wiki/Center_for_Advanced_Materials" title="Center for Advanced Materials">Center for Advanced Materials</a> in Qatar University. The program encompasses the <a href="/wiki/STEM_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="STEM fields">STEM fields</a> and languages.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">[320]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>

      </ul>

          <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r999302996"><cite id="CITEREFBoghardt2014" class="citation web cs1">Boghardt, Lori Plotkin (6 October 2014). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://newrepublic.com/article/119705/why-does-qatar-support-known-terrorists">"Qatar Is a U.S. Ally. They Also Knowingly Abet Terrorism. What's Going On?"</a>. <i>New Republic</i><span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">7 October</span> 2014</span>. <q>Two overarching goals have driven Qatari policy. One has been to maximize Qatar's influence on the regional and international stage. This originally reflected the personal ambition of the former ruler and current emir's father, Shaykh Hamad bin Khalifa al Thani, and his foreign minister and eventual prime minister, Shaykh Hamad bin Jassim al Thani. The two men directed foreign policy until the father abdicated in favor of his son, Emir Tamim bin Hamad al Thani, in July 2013. The second objective has been to preserve the security of the ruling family and state.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.jtitle=New+Republic&amp;rft.atitle=Qatar+Is+a+U.S.+Ally.+They+Also+Knowingly+Abet+Terrorism.+What%27s+Going+On%3F&amp;rft.date=2014-10-06&amp;rft.aulast=Boghardt&amp;rft.aufirst=Lori+Plotkin&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fnewrepublic.com%2Farticle%2F119705%2Fwhy-does-qatar-support-known-terrorists&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AQatar" class="Z3988"></span></span> </li>
